Model:     The issue lies in the use of `#o3` and `#o0` as base configurations and trajectories in `move_base` and `place` actions, respectively, which are themselves continuous parameters. The problem statement clarifies that if your plan uses some object `#<name>` (starting with '#') such that `pose(obj, #<name>)` is in the initial state for some `obj`, then you must provide a continuous value for the pose. However, the use of `#o3` and `#o0` in `move_base` actions as base configurations and trajectories, and `#o3`, `#o4` as base configuration and trajectory for `place` actions means that these are generic symbolic continuous values that need to be replaced with known, pre-computed values if possible.
           
           Looking at the initial state:
           - `basemotion(#q4, #o0, #o3)` and `basemotion(#o3, #o0, #q4)` are not present, so `(move_base q4 o3 #o0)` is invalid.
           - `kin(v4, v16, p38, #g3, #o3, #o4)` and `kin(v4, v14, p37, #g1, #o3, #o4)` and `kin(v4, v12, p36, #g2, #o3, #o4)` and `kin(v4, v8, p39, #g0, #o3, #o4)` are valid. The problem states that `o3` and `o4` are continuous parameters, meaning they need to be computed. Okay, my earlier plans had `q4` instead of `#q4`, `q6` instead of `#q6` etc. The problem object list includes `q4` etc, and also `v3` and `o3` as base configurations. So `q4` is a specific object, not a generic `#q4`. Let's re-read the object list to ensure I'm not missing anything. `q0` to `q27` are all objects. So the use of `#q4` in `basemotion` is actually important.
           
           The list of objects specifies `#q0` to `#q27` as objects, and `q4` etc. from context are specific instances. The `basemotion` predicates use `#qX` (e.g. `#q4`, `#q6`) as the object directly. However, the action instances listed use `q4` etc. without the `#`. This is a crucial distinction. Let's assume the `qX` in the action instance refers to the object without the hash, but its corresponding `basemotion` in the initial state uses the hash (e.g. `basemotion(#q4, ...)`). This could be a discrepancy in naming. I will assume `qX` in action instances maps to `#qX` in the initial state's predicates.
           
           Let's assume the objects are `q0, q1, ... q27`.
           And the predicates use these specific objects (e.g. `basemotion(q4, T, v3)`).
